  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_10d74af0-a233-4366-b9dc-54683b59ce79'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer657374657974953862">Nominated as one of America’s best-loved novels by PBS’s The Great American Read<br/><br/>Set in Greenwich Village, Harlem, and France, among other locales, Another Country is a novel of passions--sexual, racial, political, artistic--that is stunning for its emotional intensity and haunting sensuality, depicting men and women, blacks and whites, stripped of their masks of gender and</span>
  <span id="freeText657374657974953862" style="display:none">Nominated as one of America’s best-loved novels by PBS’s The Great American Read<br /><br />Set in Greenwich Village, Harlem, and France, among other locales, Another Country is a novel of passions--sexual, racial, political, artistic--that is stunning for its emotional intensity and haunting sensuality, depicting men and women, blacks and whites, stripped of their masks of gender and race by love and hatred at the most elemental and sublime. In a small set of friends, Baldwin imbues the best and worst intentions of liberal America in the early 1970s.</span>

        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<div id="review_407226955" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/407226955" />
    <a title="Mary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5304930-mary"><img alt="Mary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603654425p2/5304930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/407226955?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary" href="/user/show/5304930-mary">Mary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780679744719" href="/book/show/334170.Another_Country">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5304930-mary?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5304930-mary?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer407226955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17357521711307594502"><i>All for the first time, in the days when acts had no consequences and nothing was irrevocable, and love was simple and even pain had the dignity of enduring forever. It was unimaginable that time could do anything to diminish it.</i><br/><br/><i>But it was only love which could accomplish the miracle of making a life bearable – only love, and love itself mostly failed.</i><br/><br/>This is not a love story. <br/><br/>It was fitting that I read <b>Another Country</b> while camped out under the air conditioner or sweltering in the park or seeki</span>
  <span id="freeText17357521711307594502" style="display:none"><i>All for the first time, in the days when acts had no consequences and nothing was irrevocable, and love was simple and even pain had the dignity of enduring forever. It was unimaginable that time could do anything to diminish it.</i><br /><br /><i>But it was only love which could accomplish the miracle of making a life bearable – only love, and love itself mostly failed.</i><br /><br />This is not a love story. <br /><br />It was fitting that I read <b>Another Country</b> while camped out under the air conditioner or sweltering in the park or seeking solace by the ocean. The characters, too, were always seeking refuge, always trying to find some relief as they drank cheap whiskey, their skin stuck to the furniture, their foreheads damp, their worlds colliding and falling. The characters are tangled up with each other, muddled, two-faced, broken, angry, and pitiful. Baldwin created such an intense and suffocating piece. I needed a shower after each read. I needed a drink. <br /><br />Baldwin, who fled to a more liberated France while writing this book, explores another side of his home country and hometown. It’s deep summer in NYC in the 50s. There’s jazz, filth, liquor, art. The city – the country – is experiencing an undercurrent of racial tension. But not you. You’re so cool and forward thinking, right? Your circle of friends includes whites <i>and</i> blacks, see? <br /><br />But what if you’re struggling with your sexuality as well as your race? And what if you add class distinction to the list? And denial, guilt, fear? What if there’s infidelity, death, domestic violence? <br /><br />What if everybody is so damn lonely they turn to each other? Turn on each other? <br /><br />What if there was no such thing as “gay” or “straight?” <br /><br />What if you think you’re just so free and so bohemian in your middle-class apartment with your two kids and your husband’s fat paycheck and then it all comes crashing down?<br /><br />What if you never realize who you’re in love with until it’s too late?<br /><br />This book got under my skin. It penetrated my moods. It stifled me. It’s so bogged down in sorrow and anger and it never lets up for a moment. Never releases its noose-like grip on you. And I loved every uncomfortable and unbearable moment of it.<br /><br />Best book I've read all year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17357521711307594502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1219669596" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219669596" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32804270-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564311252p2/32804270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219669596?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/32804270-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32804270-michael?shelf=recs">recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32804270-michael?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219669596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7937451192869508484">Sprawling and introspective, <i>Another Country</i> explores the many forms love and longing can take. Set in Greenwich Village and Harlem during the late fifties, Baldwin’s third novel centers on the malaise and messy affairs of a small group of friends following the grisly suicide of one of the circle’s key members. Characters cheat on each other, cross class and racial boundaries, and strive for greatness even as despair threatens to consume them. Again and again they ask themselves and others wheth</span>
  <span id="freeText7937451192869508484" style="display:none">Sprawling and introspective, <i>Another Country</i> explores the many forms love and longing can take. Set in Greenwich Village and Harlem during the late fifties, Baldwin’s third novel centers on the malaise and messy affairs of a small group of friends following the grisly suicide of one of the circle’s key members. Characters cheat on each other, cross class and racial boundaries, and strive for greatness even as despair threatens to consume them. Again and again they ask themselves and others whether or not they’re loved—the question’s recited like an incantation throughout the novel’s three slow-moving sections—and with great insight Baldwin muses about the impact of social identity on romance. The end’s a bit abrupt, and the work’s not as thoughtfully plotted as his first two novels, but it’s still astounding and well worth checking out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7937451192869508484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1873403423" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1873403423" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11255849-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565547225p2/11255849.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1873403423?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/11255849-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780679744719" href="/book/show/334170.Another_Country">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=afro-american">afro-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=fav-authors">fav-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1873403423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16179864347902760205"><b>"Ne m'oublie pas," he whispered. "You are all I have in this world."</b><br/><br/><i>Don't forget me</i>. From Paris to Greenwich Village and Harlem, love traverses boundaries, inflames souls, manipulates the vulnerable, and burns each person who comes near its flames. Turbulent love is what Baldwin transcribes, the kind of love that is ignited by passion until it knows no name, has no form, except for the triangle it forms among friends. By now, my close GoodReads friends know about my reading love affair with Bald</span>
  <span id="freeText16179864347902760205" style="display:none"><b>"Ne m'oublie pas," he whispered. "You are all I have in this world."</b><br><br><i>Don't forget me</i>. From Paris to Greenwich Village and Harlem, love traverses boundaries, inflames souls, manipulates the vulnerable, and burns each person who comes near its flames. Turbulent love is what Baldwin transcribes, the kind of love that is ignited by passion until it knows no name, has no form, except for the triangle it forms among friends. By now, my close GoodReads friends know about my reading love affair with Baldwin, so I'll try to encapsulate the elation I feel when I savor his words. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485210996i/21793587.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>James Baldwin. Photograph: Ralph Gatti/AFP/Getty Images</b><br><br>This is my sixth Baldwin read. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17288631.Giovanni_s_Room" title="Giovanni's Room by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">Giovanni's Room</a>, I described, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1167154096?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">in that review</a>, how he hypnotized me with simple lyricism that entrapped. Our rendezvous usually unfolds this way. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1255819528?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a> of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17143.Go_Tell_It_on_the_Mountain" title="Go Tell It on the Mountain by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">Go Tell It on the Mountain</a>, I wrote how he gave me music in words, and I fell for each note. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38463.If_Beale_Street_Could_Talk" title="If Beale Street Could Talk by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">If Beale Street Could Talk</a> he rendered pain vivid; in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/464260.The_Fire_Next_Time" title="The Fire Next Time by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fire Next Time</a>, he warmed me, and in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/410810.Notes_of_a_Native_Son" title="Notes of a Native Son by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">Notes of a Native Son</a>, which I plan to read again soon, he gave me perspective.<br><br>In <i>Another Country,</i> he makes me ponder the profundity of love's role in self-angst, self-loathe. What happens in a person's life to make him hate himself, his skin, his people, his lover, his friend? What makes a woman use her beauty not only as a method of survival, but also as a tool for delivering hatred? What drives a secured and married mother into the hands of another? What happens when hopelessness drowns the conscious mind and sends it into self-pitying stupor? Each chapter is laced with these questions. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485210996i/21793588._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Harlem</b><br><br><b>"The light seemed to fall with an increased hardness, examining and inciting the city with an unsparing violence, like the violence of love, and striking from the city's grays and blacks a splendor as of steel on steel. In the windows of tall buildings flame wavered, alive, in ice."</b><br><br>One thing's for sure: Baldwin knows how to write about sex and angst. He elucidates despair in a way uniquely his and highlights biracial and homosexual love in a way only someone from his unique vantage point could. Here, despair lives on the streets of Harlem and Greenwich village, in the hearts of bohemians, in struggling artists and writers. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485210996i/21793589._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Greenwich Village, 1960s</b><br><br><b>"We're all unpredictable, he finally said, "one way or another. I wouldn't like you to think that you're special.<br>"It's very hard to live with that," said Eric. "I mean, with the sense that one is never what one seems-never-and yet, what one seems to be is probably, in some sense, almost exactly what one is." He turned his half-smiling face to Vivaldo. "Do you know what I mean?"<br>"I wish I didn't," said Vivaldo, slowly,"but I'm afraid I do."</b><br><br>The first eighty-eight pages of this book could have been a novella. No one could read this first part and love Rufus, for even Rufus didn't love Rufus. Pained as he was, he took it out on Leona, a young white woman who escaped a painful past from the South, only to find herself in a tumultuous relationship with him. The first part is a novella cold and hostile, laced with self-hatred, but it exists to make lucid the gritty world of racism and segregation, a world wherein each character connected to Rufus resides within some self-revelatory cocoon he or she must be released from. There is Cass, wife of the writer, Richard; Eric, the American actor who has returned from Paris; Ida, Rufus' sister who becomes his friend's lover, and Vivaldo, Rufus' best friend and the white man whose perspective Baldwin uses to inspect race relations. Vivaldo was my favorite character. <br><br><i>Don't forget me</i>, it's as if the phrase is embedded within each sentence spoken, within each unforgivable gesture. Love, lust, and angst engulf these pages and turn thunderous. Relationships are mangled and mutilated, and one wonders if anything is what it seems. As the sections progress, erotic savagery culminates into hungry lovemaking and misguided lust turns into uncertain love that is<br><blockquote>buried beneath the impossible language of the time, lived underground where nearly all of the time's true feeling spitefully and incessantly fermented.</blockquote><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16179864347902760205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2673585943" />
    <a title="Rosh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67389060-rosh"><img alt="Rosh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522427732p2/67389060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2673585943?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosh" href="/user/show/67389060-rosh">Rosh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2673585943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12933652381351297527">It took 15 years for Baldwin to complete this novel. He travelled all across from Paris to Turkey in poor health, depressed, and feeling that he had lost sight of his aims as a writer. On the brink of suicide, this novel had almost killed him. And while reading this you can sense Baldwin's sense of despair, torment and rage.<br/><br/>This would not be a Baldwin novel if he did not deal with social issues such as race, class, and same sex relationships. Baldwin has a way of eloquently showing people's ugly</span>
  <span id="freeText12933652381351297527" style="display:none">It took 15 years for Baldwin to complete this novel. He travelled all across from Paris to Turkey in poor health, depressed, and feeling that he had lost sight of his aims as a writer. On the brink of suicide, this novel had almost killed him. And while reading this you can sense Baldwin's sense of despair, torment and rage.<br /><br />This would not be a Baldwin novel if he did not deal with social issues such as race, class, and same sex relationships. Baldwin has a way of eloquently showing people's ugly core as they deal with such issues. He doesn't allow any character to simply get by but he makes them face and confront their weaknesses and lies. <br /><br />A large and relevant piece of America can be inspected here. I hesitate about stars. I certainly don't 'love' the book on 5 star level. Do I 'like' it enough for 4? Does respect and tempered admiration justify 4?<br /></span>

<div id="review_75957093" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75957093" />
    <a title="Jesse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1432036-jesse"><img alt="Jesse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544746042p2/1432036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75957093?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesse" href="/user/show/1432036-jesse">Jesse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440302001" href="/book/show/1436864.Another_Country">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1432036-jesse?shelf=1960-s">1960-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1432036-jesse?shelf=authors-of-color">authors-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1432036-jesse?shelf=queer-lit">queer-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1432036-jesse?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1432036-jesse?shelf=american-lit">american-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1432036-jesse?shelf=formative">formative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1432036-jesse?shelf=in-the-village">in-the-village</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1432036-jesse?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75957093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7794399036671673613">Wow. Just... <i>wow</i>. Kind of weird—my reaction is not declare <i>Another Country</i> a new favorite, I just didn't love it in that way. And yet, and yet, it penetrated deeply, perhaps more deeply than some books I do consider my favorite...<br/><br/>Perhaps this has to do with how perplexing Baldwin is as an author—it takes a while, almost too much effort to get into the story, and then suddenly, unexpectedly you're in an ever-tightening vice, not sure how the hell Baldwin got you there before you even managed to n</span>
  <span id="freeText7794399036671673613" style="display:none">Wow. Just... <i>wow</i>. Kind of weird—my reaction is not declare <i>Another Country</i> a new favorite, I just didn't love it in that way. And yet, and yet, it penetrated deeply, perhaps more deeply than some books I do consider my favorite...<br /><br />Perhaps this has to do with how perplexing Baldwin is as an author—it takes a while, almost too much effort to get into the story, and then suddenly, unexpectedly you're in an ever-tightening vice, not sure how the hell Baldwin got you there before you even managed to notice. He certainly has a way with words, beautiful, almost aggressively lyrical without ever being showy; but what his words <i>do</i> have is weight, an almost unbearable density that in some passages seem to weigh so heavily upon the skin, as if their sole purpose is to rip to shreds any layers of resistance, pick apart any and every last defense...<br /><br />Really, I suppose that's as good a description as any of what Baldwin does to his characters; he flays them alive so their intangible insides—their hopes, fears, secrets, contradictions, prejudices, dreams—are splayed unceremoniously upon dirty Greenwich Village sidewalks and greasy tables in the smoky corners of dive bars for each other to see, to gawk at, to pick ruthlessly at, to take up and wield like weapons to destroy each other, to bind each other closer than ever before...<br /><br />And to take it one step further—the title kind of demands as much—the same could be said about Baldwin's general examination of America: mercilessly yet lovingly (the oh-so-thin line separating love from hate is a reoccurring preoccupation throughout the book) ripping the American psyche apart. Granted, his focus on a very particular group, mid-to-late 50's Greenwich Village, certainly one of the most socially progressive enclaves in society at that time. But that's almost what makes Baldwin's exposé so very painful—he's unearthing and then brutally exposing the most hidden prejudices of the particular kind (regarding race, gender, class, sexuality) that liberals and artistic types like to think they've managed to exorcise and escape from. Baldwin's indictment of white liberal guilt can be particularly agonizing...<br /><br />Kind of hopeless (the constant refrain at our first bookclub discussion: "it's amazing how so little has changed..."), but oh, so very necessary. Anybody who claims we live in a post-racial, post-<i>anything</i> era here in America needs to be promptly slapped upside the head with this book. <br /><br /><br /><i>"Perhaps such secrets, the secrets of everyone, were only expressed when the person laboriously dragged them into the light of the world, imposed them on the world, and made them a part of the world's experience. Without this effort, the secret place was merely a dungeon in which the person perished; without this effort, indeed, the entire world would be an uninhabitable darkness; and she saw, with a dreadful reluctance, why this effort was so rare."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7794399036671673613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2026169004" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2026169004" />
    <a title="Faith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17430801-faith"><img alt="Faith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372868249p2/17430801.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2026169004?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith" href="/user/show/17430801-faith">Faith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17430801-faith?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17430801-faith?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2026169004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14913438432218652532">I am appalled that it took me so long to read Baldwin, but I am gradually correcting my outrageous neglect of this important author. He was a tremendously skillful writer. This character-driven book is about a group of authors, musicians, actors and a few others who come together in New York City. They are male, female, black, white, heterosexual and bisexual. They love, hurt, attract, challenge and repel each other in various combinations. They also struggle with issues surrounding their career</span>
  <span id="freeText14913438432218652532" style="display:none">I am appalled that it took me so long to read Baldwin, but I am gradually correcting my outrageous neglect of this important author. He was a tremendously skillful writer. This character-driven book is about a group of authors, musicians, actors and a few others who come together in New York City. They are male, female, black, white, heterosexual and bisexual. They love, hurt, attract, challenge and repel each other in various combinations. They also struggle with issues surrounding their careers, families, race and sexuality. <br /><br />There is a staccato rhythm to this book. Although it is not plot-driven, the book moves along very quickly. Baldwin was a master observer. It felt like he had spent hours watching people both alone and interacting in bars, funerals, apartments and on the street. He eavesdropped on conversations and looked through windows. There is clarity in both his observations and his precise use of language. The book ended abruptly and I really wanted to know what happened next to these people.<br /><br />The narration by Dion Graham of the audiobook was excellent. He even sings well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14913438432218652532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText226715604622631113" style="display:none">I don't even know where to begin with Another Country.....<br /><br />This book showed me myself in ways I had never imagined a book could....I mean talk about intense, raw, truth, hurt, love, booze, swinging, and every other action that connects all human beings...<br /><br />I am 21 years old, and to think that December 10th if this year will mark the 50th Anniversary of this book is mind-blowing to me.<br /><br />I first have to start with Rufus Scott....I have never had a character in fiction who was complex, and damaged that I could FEEL like this young man.....The funeral scene where the pastor is eulogizing Rufus is by far one of my most powerful moment's in reading I have had...I being a african American truly have been to funerals like this my life.<br /><br /> Now with the other person who I truly connected with was Eric....I found Eric to vulnerable, real, human...One of my most favorite quotes comes from Eric talking about his relationship with Yves, and how being homosexual in an era where that it was not accepted, and with that has the background he goes on talking about because of his desires, he found himself living a 'secret life' where he goes on to say to me one of the most profound life mantras..." <div id="review_1090863162" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090863162" />
    <a title="l." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3065234-l"><img alt="l." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555529602p2/3065234.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1090863162?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="l." class="user" itemprop="url" name="l." href="/user/show/3065234-l">l.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3065234-l?shelf=novel-novella">novel-novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3065234-l?shelf=american-lit">american-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3065234-l?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3065234-l?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1090863162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4095064388364645587">Something about Baldwin's writing doesn't quite work for me and I wasn't sure what it was until I read this book; it's the centrality of male pain. Despite what Ida goes through, it's Rufus' death that is privileged, Rufus' hardship that shapes how Ida views her life, more than her own experiences. It's Rufus' death that is the crux of Baldwin's condemnation of America. The only character who dislikes Rufus for beating up his white southern girlfriend is Richard, the least sympathetic, least fle</span>
  <span id="freeText4095064388364645587" style="display:none">Something about Baldwin's writing doesn't quite work for me and I wasn't sure what it was until I read this book; it's the centrality of male pain. Despite what Ida goes through, it's Rufus' death that is privileged, Rufus' hardship that shapes how Ida views her life, more than her own experiences. It's Rufus' death that is the crux of Baldwin's condemnation of America. The only character who dislikes Rufus for beating up his white southern girlfriend is Richard, the least sympathetic, least fleshed out character in the book. Ida is actually Rufus' chief hagiographer - calling the girlfriend a crazy cracker/bitch who ruined a great man. <a href="http://theculture.forharriet.com/2014/03/revolutionary-hope-conversation-between.html" rel="nofollow noopener">In an interview with Audre Lorde</a>, Baldwin draws a distinction between 'responsibility' and 'fault' - a black man in America who commits an offense is responsible but not at fault. I don't agree with his use of those words, but I understand his point. So does Audre Lorde - she agrees with most of what Baldwin is saying but attempts to make him recognize that black men have a place in the power hierarchy as well - specifically in the oppression of black women. Given the harassment that Ida receives from black men for dating white men, you would think this would not be a point of contention among them, but Baldwin just doesn't get it. He speaks over Lorde, saying: "How can you be so sentimental as to blame the Black man for a situation which has nothing to do with him?" He also says that the 'only' crime in America is to be born a black male - "It's not like being a woman." OIC. I'm underwhelmed by this, but I'm glad that I was picking up on something that was actually there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4095064388364645587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3415391151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3415391151" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3415391151?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2020-shelf">2020-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=traditional-fiction">traditional-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3415391151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8651638754851162605">This is one of those novels, like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38462.Giovanni_s_Room' title='Giovanni's Room by James Baldwin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Giovanni's Room</a> that dives deep into interpersonal relationships in a very deep and broad way. Not only is it about the complicated relationships between blacks and whites, but about m/m, m/f, and all the messy complicated issues that can happen between them all. <br/><br/>Yes, it's about racism, but mostly it's about fairly decent people trying to make it work and still getting it all wrong. And that's interesting, no? For a book that came out in 1962, he runs through th</span>
  <span id="freeText8651638754851162605" style="display:none">This is one of those novels, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38462.Giovanni_s_Room" title="Giovanni's Room by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">Giovanni's Room</a> that dives deep into interpersonal relationships in a very deep and broad way. Not only is it about the complicated relationships between blacks and whites, but about m/m, m/f, and all the messy complicated issues that can happen between them all. <br /><br />Yes, it's about racism, but mostly it's about fairly decent people trying to make it work and still getting it all wrong. And that's interesting, no? For a book that came out in 1962, he runs through the whole gamut of human interaction and it's often sweet, scary, idealistic, depressing, and sometimes downright ugly.<br /><br />But it's also not overblown or politicized. And that's INTERESTING, to me. It's very modern without being ugly-modern. Where everyone has an agenda, Baldwin seems free of it. <br /><br />I mean... assuming you already think that humans are a chaotic heap that can mess itself up quite nicely without outside influence. :)<br /><br />Very interesting novel. It belongs right up there with all the human-nature greats. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8651638754851162605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3415391151">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_2467738230" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2467738230" />
    <a title="Teresa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/541416-teresa"><img alt="Teresa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570841350p2/541416.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2467738230?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teresa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teresa" href="/user/show/541416-teresa">Teresa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440302001" href="/book/show/1436864.Another_Country">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2467738230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer697001168841709340"><b>4.5</b><br/><br/>Near the start of this book, I was reminded of Baldwin’s previous novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38462.Giovanni_s_Room' title='Giovanni's Room by James Baldwin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Giovanni's Room</a>. But it quickly becomes <i>Giovanni’s Room</i>-‘exploded’, for this is not just the story of fraught tension between a homosexual man and a possibly bisexual man; but also the story of other couples, and coupling: a white woman who has escaped the South and a black man; a white man and a black woman; and, the one that seemed the most forced to me, an ‘older’ married woman and a homosexual (bisexual?) man, anothe</span>
  <span id="freeText697001168841709340" style="display:none"><b>4.5</b><br /><br />Near the start of this book, I was reminded of Baldwin’s previous novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38462.Giovanni_s_Room" title="Giovanni's Room by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">Giovanni's Room</a>. But it quickly becomes <i>Giovanni’s Room</i>-‘exploded’, for this is not just the story of fraught tension between a homosexual man and a possibly bisexual man; but also the story of other couples, and coupling: a white woman who has escaped the South and a black man; a white man and a black woman; and, the one that seemed the most forced to me, an ‘older’ married woman and a homosexual (bisexual?) man, another escaped Southerner. Ultimately, Baldwin seems to be commenting on the uselessness of such sexual labels, that these relationships are all due to love, or at least something approximating it—and any hate arising between the couple is due to cultural discrimination and pasts that may be impossible to overcome. <br /><br />Through the characters’ thoughts and words, rendered in beautiful prose, the intricacies of the various relationships are empathetically delineated, in both their joy and their violence. “Violence” is a word Baldwin uses in interesting, and unexpected, ways throughout the work, such as using it as a collective noun. <br /><br />“Towers” (skyscrapers) loom over the inhabitants of New York City, seeming to doom them. That image is carried over to France, with the towers of Chartres Cathedral serving the same function for a visiting couple consummating their relationship. Despite the plot’s brief sojourn to France, I am left with the feeling that the city of New York, more so than any of the characters, is the primary, motivating force of the work; even more so than the character from the first section who links the others.<br /><br />With its frank depictions of sexuality (never seeming gratuitous), the casual use of marijuana and themes that have remained relevant, I had to keep reminding myself this was published in the very early 60s.</span>
  <a data-text-id="697001168841709340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josh" href="/user/show/6041973-josh">Josh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer841870410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9762918245805412525">The first chapter is what makes this book: 88 pages of astonishing sadness, the amazing elucidation of the painful psyche of main character Rufus and could easily be a standalone novella/short story in Baldwin's remarkable oeuvre; perhaps one of the <i>best</i> short stories about the human psyche I've come across so far. <br/><br/>This chapter sets up for what's to follow; more pain, more self-analysis of what it means to be of color, what it means to loathe the opposite or the oppressor, to loathe yourself for</span>
  <span id="freeText9762918245805412525" style="display:none">The first chapter is what makes this book: 88 pages of astonishing sadness, the amazing elucidation of the painful psyche of main character Rufus and could easily be a standalone novella/short story in Baldwin's remarkable oeuvre; perhaps one of the <i>best</i> short stories about the human psyche I've come across so far. <br /><br />This chapter sets up for what's to follow; more pain, more self-analysis of what it means to be of color, what it means to loathe the opposite or the oppressor, to loathe yourself for who you are and what you are and what you're attracted to, but to accept it, warily, each day until you take your last breath. <br /><br />Baldwin's rhetoric formulates questions that you want to answer, but often cannot, but follow closely and intimately. Such beautiful writing as always. Read this for the first chapter alone.</span>

<div id="review_1876176277" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Lauren " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1291915-lauren"><img alt="Lauren " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604235645p2/1291915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1876176277?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren " href="/user/show/1291915-lauren">Lauren </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440302001" href="/book/show/1436864.Another_Country">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=book-club-selections">book-club-selections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=1960s-fiction">1960s-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291915-lauren?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1876176277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3074764694771168518">Baldwin spent 13 years writing ANOTHER COUNTRY. He stated that the characters fell silent, stopped talking to him, so he let them rest and focused on his prolific and defining essays and commentaries, as well as his own travels through Europe, Africa, and Asia. <br/><br/>In some ways, the span of time it took to write it is evident. There are tonal shifts in this book, most notably a "set piece" in the first 80ish-pages, following the character Rufus, inspired by one of Baldwin's friends. The book sprawls</span>
  <span id="freeText3074764694771168518" style="display:none">Baldwin spent 13 years writing ANOTHER COUNTRY. He stated that the characters fell silent, stopped talking to him, so he let them rest and focused on his prolific and defining essays and commentaries, as well as his own travels through Europe, Africa, and Asia. <br /><br />In some ways, the span of time it took to write it is evident. There are tonal shifts in this book, most notably a "set piece" in the first 80ish-pages, following the character Rufus, inspired by one of Baldwin's friends. The book sprawls over time and space, as well as character motivations and actions. It reflects a changing Harlem, with migration of southern African-Americans, immigration of Europeans to New York, class and generational conflicts, and the bohemian life of artists, writers, and musicians who have a lot of sex and do a lot of dope.<br /><br />The jazz bars are a key setting in this story. Characters live in these spaces, perform in them, drink excessively in them. Hook up and break ups. Much of the ink of 320 pages is the intricate conversations and observations in this world. It's character-driven at its core. It's groundbreaking in its themes, but beautifully rendered with equal parts compassion and rage.<br /><br />It's subtle, and it's sublime.<br /><br />My second novel by Baldwin - I read his earlier work Giovonni's Room several years ago - and this one is deeper, but also bigger in scope.<br /><br />I read and reread paragraphs and pages of this book. It seemed like Baldwin had the ability to stop time and give the reader 360° of access to this world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3074764694771168518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1997767444?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/48502194-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780679744719" href="/book/show/334170.Another_Country">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48502194-kathleen?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1997767444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4211414187892973544"><i>“But it was only love which could accomplish the miracle of making a life bearable—only love, and love itself mostly failed …”</i><br/><br/>Have you ever had somebody tell you something, something secret and maybe a bit shocking but at the same time familiar and it makes you see them for who they are and that brings up these tender feelings for them that you didn’t know you had and after that you look at them and yourself and the whole world differently? That’s <i>Another Country</i>. <br/><br/>This is my first reading of Bal</span>
  <span id="freeText4211414187892973544" style="display:none"><i>“But it was only love which could accomplish the miracle of making a life bearable—only love, and love itself mostly failed …”</i><br /><br />Have you ever had somebody tell you something, something secret and maybe a bit shocking but at the same time familiar and it makes you see them for who they are and that brings up these tender feelings for them that you didn’t know you had and after that you look at them and yourself and the whole world differently? That’s <i>Another Country</i>. <br /><br />This is my first reading of Baldwin’s fiction. He mined for truth and brought back gems in his non-fiction writing, and I shouldn’t have been surprised that he did the same with his fiction, but the way he did it was fascinating to me. He goes back and forth through the lives of these characters like he’s uncoiling a spring. And he gives us the characters’ minds and bodies through details of movement as well as thought that go beyond anything I’ve read before. He forces me to inhabit them. <br /><br /><i>“His fingers, at her waist, seemed to have become abnormally and dangerously sensitive, and he prayed that his face did not show the enormous, illicit pleasure which entered him through his fingertips.”</i><br /><br />This story is uncomfortable, gritty, raw, desperate, sad, life-affirming, and real. <br /><br /><i>“Don’t let it make you bitter. Try to understand. Try to understand. The world’s already bitter enough, we got to try to be better than the world.”</i></span>

<div id="review_1342209320" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1342209320" />
    <a title="Sian Griffiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16212916-sian-griffiths"><img alt="Sian Griffiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594948872p2/16212916.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1342209320?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sian Griffiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sian Griffiths" href="/user/show/16212916-sian-griffiths">Sian Griffiths</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1342209320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14341262891736794702">I wanted to love this book so much more than I did. I deeply admire Baldwin's bravery in tackling the subjects of systemic racism and socially forbidden love, and some of the sentences took my breath away with their beautiful construction. Even so, the book is veined with a deep-seated misogyny. Women here are either weak or "bitches," and either way they seem to want to be slapped around. Ugh. The characters in general feel thin to me, like figures created to drive a plot and propose theories o</span>
  <span id="freeText14341262891736794702" style="display:none">I wanted to love this book so much more than I did. I deeply admire Baldwin's bravery in tackling the subjects of systemic racism and socially forbidden love, and some of the sentences took my breath away with their beautiful construction. Even so, the book is veined with a deep-seated misogyny. Women here are either weak or "bitches," and either way they seem to want to be slapped around. Ugh. The characters in general feel thin to me, like figures created to drive a plot and propose theories of the world rather than real people taking real action driven by their desire and individual personality. Each seems to speak with the same voice. The shifting point of view didn't help, and at the end, I had no idea whose story this was or what I was supposed to take from it except that love is inflammatory and destructive, a theory I'm not quite willing to buy. In this novel, Baldwin is at his best when writing about the love between men. There is real beauty here, but in the end, for me at least, the novel's beauty wasn't enough to overcome its woman hating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14341262891736794702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2887811133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2887811133" />
    <a title="Daniel Chaikin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18695911-daniel-chaikin"><img alt="Daniel Chaikin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534027159p2/18695911.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2887811133?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Chaikin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Chaikin" href="/user/show/18695911-daniel-chaikin">Daniel Chaikin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/269920.Another_Country">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2887811133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2645487357059254438">My Litsy post, written just as I finished: <i>Finished on my way out of town. Seems Baldwin aims to shock and had bought into Freud. Often called pornographic, there is a lot of sex in detail... sometimes it‘s beautiful, but it‘s always uncomfortable and it‘s never the point. He‘s looking at sexuality, race, psychology, and at the loneliness within the unnatural landscape of the heart of Manhattan. The books a mash, too much. Runs and sputters, fades, returns, irritating and powerful.</i><br/><br/>I had a strong</span>
  <span id="freeText2645487357059254438" style="display:none">My Litsy post, written just as I finished: <i>Finished on my way out of town. Seems Baldwin aims to shock and had bought into Freud. Often called pornographic, there is a lot of sex in detail... sometimes it‘s beautiful, but it‘s always uncomfortable and it‘s never the point. He‘s looking at sexuality, race, psychology, and at the loneliness within the unnatural landscape of the heart of Manhattan. The books a mash, too much. Runs and sputters, fades, returns, irritating and powerful.</i><br /><br />I had a strong opinion on finishing, so glad I captured a little of my mood in the Litsy review. I got too busy to review and now it's...well, it has a different feel. The hard lines have softened and my sense of the book has mellowed overall, both on what I didn't like and what I liked. I even changed my rating up ½ a star. <br /><br />Apologies to short attention spans (I have one too) but I need to slow this down a bit. When Baldwin was asked about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38462.Giovanni_s_Room" title="Giovanni’s Room by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">Giovanni’s Room</a>, a high profile openly and beautifully gay novel, he was asked why he didn't address racism, since his reputation was as a "negro" writer who wrote about racism (yes, the question is racist). He said it was too much, in one book, to address racism and homosexuality. He apparently changed his mind, or, the world was just rapidly changing in this era. A black bisexual musician, Rufus, opens this book and his homosexuality, his interracial relationships, his blackness and a variety of perspectives on race issues are only some of the "shock" elements in this book. It's a lot for one book.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38474.Another_Country" title="Another Country by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">Another Country</a> is a book commonly banned, especially from schools, because it's considered pornographic. The opening is a play-by-play, emotion-by-emotion sex scene. (It's one of the most beautiful scenes in the book.) It's not exactly an unfair assessment, although Baldwin would disagree. He was trying to shock anyone uncomfortable with the various sexual connections he comes up with. Regardless of his purpose, sex is a tough way to drive a plot and the pace of this book is all over the place, dreamy here, fast here, slow and really dull there. It would have been an easy book to give up halfway through. Ultimately it's really rewarding; a character driven, thought-provoking look at many different things, especially at life in Manhattan and the loneliness of being in the midst of all those buildings and people. <br /><br />On closing the book I was thinking a lot about the pace and about some sex scenes that really bothered me, and about some that were really beautiful. As the bright colors faded over this past week, I'm left with mainly the beautiful impressions, the dreamy quality and tenderness with which Baldwin creates his characters. An outrageous personality, nothing is simple with Baldwin, but he seems to have a little longing for some unobtainable peaceful simplicity. <br /><br />Recommended for fans of Baldwin who have already read Giovanni's Room know this book is too busy to be anywhere as good as that one was, but still maybe has its own lingering power.<br /><br />-----------------------------------------------<br /><br />34. <b>Another Country by James Baldwin</b><br /><b>published</b>: 1962<br /><b>format</b>: 390 pages inside <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38456.Early_Novels___Stories_Go_Tell_It_on_the_Mountain___Giovanni_s_Room___Another_Country___Going_to_Meet_the_Man" title="Early Novels &amp; Stories Go Tell It on the Mountain / Giovanni’s Room / Another Country / Going to Meet the Man by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">Early Novels &amp; Stories: Go Tell It on the Mountain / Giovanni’s Room / Another Country / Going to Meet the Man</a><br /><b>acquired</b>: December<br /><b>read</b>: Jul 7-26<br /><b>time reading</b>: 14 hr 12 min, 2.2 min/page<br /><b>rating</b>: 4</span>
  <a data-text-id="2645487357059254438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1300516839" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1300516839" />
    <a title="Maya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23315852-maya"><img alt="Maya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420461364p2/23315852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1300516839?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maya" href="/user/show/23315852-maya">Maya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19169401-another-country">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1300516839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5233496241136868192"><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"Nobody – no man and no woman – is precisely what they think they are. Love is where you find it. And you don’t know where it will carry you. And it's a terrifying thing. Love - it’s the only human possibility but it’s terrifying. <br/>[…]<br/>If you can’t love anybody you are dangerous because you’ve no way of learning humility."</b>
</blockquote><br/>Excerpt from an interview with James Baldwin. <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XZPmT3lk6cU' rel='nofollow noopener'>Source: Youtube</a> <br/><br/>Although this interview wasn’t specifically related to Another Country I felt what James Baldwin said there summ</span>
  <span id="freeText5233496241136868192" style="display:none"><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"Nobody – no man and no woman – is precisely what they think they are. Love is where you find it. And you don’t know where it will carry you. And it's a terrifying thing. Love - it’s the only human possibility but it’s terrifying. <br />[…]<br />If you can’t love anybody you are dangerous because you’ve no way of learning humility."</b>
</blockquote><br />Excerpt from an interview with James Baldwin. <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XZPmT3lk6cU" rel="nofollow noopener">Source: Youtube</a> <br /><br />Although this interview wasn’t specifically related to Another Country I felt what James Baldwin said there summarizes the book quite well.<br /><br />It’s a story about a group of friends looking for their true selves and for true love in a place evolving so quickly and in a time when everything was changing so fast – New York city in the late 1950s - that they were constantly lost. Yet, to some of them it seemed that what most mattered would never change as the past had its claws too deep into the present. So they couldn’t change as well. <br /><br />Still, they all wanted to be something they were not but each of them had a weakness which turned out to be too big of an obstacle. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“It’s very hard to live with that,” said Eric. “I mean, with the sense that one is never what one seems— never— and yet, what one seems to be is probably, in some sense, almost exactly what one is.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Because of how James Baldwin wrote the characters in Another Country – merciless to their weaknesses but compassionate to their failures at the same time – I didn’t have high hopes for a happy ending although there were sparks of happiness and moments when the loneliness was forgotten not just at the bottom of an empty bourbon bottle but in the embrace of a true friend. But it was never enough. And even though he pushed them relentlessly until they hit the bottom there was never judgment or taking sides from him – just the raw truth. So when they acted selfishly – with no care for the consequences – grabbing whatever pieces of love they found on their way, I could not find it in me to judge either.<br /><br />Racism and discrimination are main themes in the book. I could see how much Baldwin’s heart bled on the pages of this book, and because I don’t feel competent enough to delve into these issues here I’d only say that he did show - over 50 years ago - that regardless of race, gender, sexual orientation, social status – all people love, hate, and suffer the same way. <br /><br /><br />4.5 stars<br /><br /><br />BR with Sofia - July 17, 2015. Our chat with spoilers <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/read_statuses/935189177?comment=137203741#comment_137203741" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5233496241136868192" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1301095451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301095451" />
    <a title="Sofia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14453898-sofia"><img alt="Sofia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404331721p2/14453898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1301095451?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia" href="/user/show/14453898-sofia">Sofia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19169401-another-country">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14453898-sofia?shelf=3-5-stars">3-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1301095451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7575469170374456829">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Baldwin gave me a lonely, desolate, angry, violent vision of New York from the point of view of a group of liberal artists and how they lived the racial tension between blacks and whites. In their turn they had to deal with conflict that showed how much or how not so liberal they were. Their search for meaning, love, connection was and is universal regardless of race. But racial/historical differences will raise their ugly heads. I might say that this story is about something that happe</span>
  <span id="freeText7575469170374456829" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Baldwin gave me a lonely, desolate, angry, violent vision of New York from the point of view of a group of liberal artists and how they lived the racial tension between blacks and whites. In their turn they had to deal with conflict that showed how much or how not so liberal they were. Their search for meaning, love, connection was and is universal regardless of race. But racial/historical differences will raise their ugly heads. I might say that this story is about something that happened back there in the 50/60’s far away in America. But I cannot because the same things are still happening in America and in my backyard with the thousands escaping from the war torn Middle East and North Africa into our own island and the rest of Europe. So it’s not far away and still relevant.<br /><br />I may never grasp what being black means but this little bit that Baldwin gives me is a piece that helps keep the mind open to different realities than mine. Did I enjoy the journey? – well considering the feelings it kindled, no, not so much. I wanted to get the sad feeling it created over and done with. The sad truth is that I can close the book and it ends there for me but there is no possibility of doing that for the people whose reality it represents. <br /><br />I had really enjoyed reading Baldwin’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/876411421?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Giovanni’s Room</a> which was compact and excellently crafted in my opinion, so I was a bit disappointed that I did not find this one not so compelling. Oh the writing is crafty but not so compact as Giovanni’s Room, so this created gaps of boredom at my end. I think I appreciate this more for the thoughts I had in its wake and the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/read_statuses/935189177?comment=137404099&amp;page=2#comment_137404099&lt;br /&gt;" rel="nofollow noopener">chats</a> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1300516839" rel="nofollow noopener">Maya</a> about the points it raised for both of us.<br /> <br /><br />Read with Maya - our 2nd Baldwin read<br /> 		 	 	 	 	 <br />	<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7575469170374456829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Vince" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/587238-vince"><img alt="Vince" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23084460?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vince" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vince" href="/user/show/587238-vince">Vince</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of Great Literature</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23084460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9126432839100748057">A relentless, searching, profound novel. Much is dated, but that's okay for readers such as I, with anthropological tendencies, i.e., old Times Square hustler argot, 50s slang -- but AC also fills in the gaps, it shows how thing were done then, the whites who went to (gasp!), private negro jazz improvs, 50s publishing circles, etc.<br/><br/>The structure as mentioned, is innovative: the loss of a person seen through a cast of characters who run the gamut; literarary, successful, unsuccessful, rich, poor, </span>
  <span id="freeText9126432839100748057" style="display:none">A relentless, searching, profound novel. Much is dated, but that's okay for readers such as I, with anthropological tendencies, i.e., old Times Square hustler argot, 50s slang -- but AC also fills in the gaps, it shows how thing were done then, the whites who went to (gasp!), private negro jazz improvs, 50s publishing circles, etc.<br /><br />The structure as mentioned, is innovative: the loss of a person seen through a cast of characters who run the gamut; literarary, successful, unsuccessful, rich, poor, black, white, gay, straight, priviledged, unprivileged. There is also a lot of bisexuality in this novel,while not being the focus of the novel. I'm sure bisexuality and homosexuality were tabu at the time. <br /><br />Note how many printings this went through. This was a SIZZLING best-seller. I've read other Baldwiin and couldn't get into some, like Go Tell It On The Mountain, but not this one. He is just a very profound, poetic writer in this one, one who goes WAY down in the soul, roots around and does NOT necessarily find the answers. Yes, it is pessimistic, I believe, overall, in positing that blacks and whites may not truly mesh or understand one another, even in a sexual relationship, and in a broader sense, in America. Time has proven him right on that one too. It is optimistic in showing how we all impact one another, or did, despite all the segregation of the times. <br /><br />He was a big intellectual. Sharp as a tack, to quote Gore Vidal, poetic and political. He's not a show-off as far as words are concerned, he's a show off in plumbing deep into the depths of the psyche, motivations, stereotypes, what's really happening, etc.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9126432839100748057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
